Traditionally, you would build a container within Docker with your code changes, push it, wait for it to upload, deploy the changes, verify them, view them, and repeat that process as you continually test your changes. Telepresence makes it a fast process by directing cluster traffic to your local container.</p>     <h1>How do I use it?</h1>     <ul>     <li><p><b>Connect your cluster to access remote services</b><br>Establish a connection with your remote Kubernetes cluster by selecting the kubeconfig and instantly access remote services from any Docker container on the host network.</p></li>     <li><p><b>Selectively route traffic by creating [0xffffffe2][0xffffff80][0xffffff9c]intercepts[0xffffffe2][0xffffff80][0xffffff9d] and manage them in Docker</b><br>Choose a target namespace and re-route, or [0xffffffe2][0xffffff80][0xffffff9c]intercept[0xffffffe2][0xffffff80][0xffffff9d], a specific service by clicking the [0xffffffe2][0xffffff80][0xffffff9c]Intercept[0xffffffe2][0xffffff80][0xffffff9d] button. Run multiple intercepts, view the list of your intercepted services and their respective namespaces and ports, and manage and keep track of all your intercepts via the Docker UI.</p></li>     <li><p><b>Preview and share your changes before deploying</b><br>Share progress with teammates and stakeholders for quick feedback based on your local code changes: generate shareable and secure URLs to preview your application before you deploy!</p></li>     </ul>     <h1>About Ambassador</h1>     <p>Ambassador Labs builds developer infrastructure that help organizations of every size to adapt to the cloud world.
